                  <foreign lang="ar">تَرَابِيع</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">quadrangular forms</hi> (in the CK <foreign lang="ar">تَرْبِيع</foreign>)] <hi rend="ital">like the eyes of wild animals.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  A bull <hi rend="ital">having a blackness between his eyes:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">a bull;</hi> so called because of the largeness of his eyes: or so called because <hi rend="ital">having spots of black and white, as though there were eyes upon his skin.</hi> (Ham p. 293.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <pb n="2219"/> And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  Locusts (<foreign lang="ar">جَرَاد</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">which, when stripped of the integument, are seen to be white and red:</hi> mentioned by Az in art. <foreign lang="ar">ينع</foreign>, on the authority of ISh. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  [Also, as pass. part. n. of 2, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Individuated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">particularized;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">distinguished from the generality,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">aggregate:</hi> &amp;c.: see the verb.
